href="#cite_note-AIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Athens International Airport <i>Eleftherios Venizelos</i></b> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x94\xce\xb9\xce\xb5\xce\xb8\xce\xbd\xce\xae\xcf\x82 \xce\x91\xce\xb5\xcf\x81\xce\xbf\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xce\xbc\xce\xad\xce\xbd\xce\xb1\xcf\x82 \xce\x91\xce\xb8\xce\xb7\xce\xbd\xcf\x8e\xce\xbd \xc2\xab\xce\x95\xce\xbb\xce\xb5\xcf\x85\xce\xb8\xce\xad\xcf\x81\xce\xb9\xce\xbf\xcf\x82 \xce\x92\xce\xb5\xce\xbd\xce\xb9\xce\xb6\xce\xad\xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xcf\x82\xc2\xbb</span>, <i>Diethn\xc3\xads Aerolim\xc3\xa9nas Athin\xc3\xb3n "Elefth\xc3\xa9rios Veniz\xc3\xa9los"</i>), commonly initialised as <b>AIA</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>ATH</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LGAV</b>), is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Greece" title="List of the busiest airports in Greece">largest international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, serving the city of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> and region of <a href="/wiki/Attica_(region)" title="Attica (region)">Attica</a>. It began operation on 28 March 2001 (in time for the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>) and is the main base of <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a>, as well as other smaller Greek airlines. It replaced the old <a href="/wiki/Ellinikon_International_Airport" title="Ellinikon International Airport">Ellinikon International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>  Athens International is currently a member of Group 1 of <a href="/wiki/Airports_Council_International" title="Airports Council International">Airports Council International</a> (over 25 million)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> as of 2020, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">19th-busiest airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_and_ownership">Development and ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development and ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Athens_International_Airport_(juillet_2000)_-_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg/220px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg/330px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg/440px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7198" data-file-height="4705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Athens_International_Airport_(juillet_2000)_-_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Athens International Airport under construction in June 2000</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Athens_International_Airport_(juillet_2000)_-_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg/220px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg/330px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg/440px-New_Athens_International_Airport_%28juillet_2000%29_-_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7198" data-file-height="4705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Athens_International_Airport_(juillet_2000)_-_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal VOR/DME at Athens International Airport</div></div></div>\n<p>AIA is located between the towns of <a href="/wiki/Markopoulo_Mesogaias" title="Markopoulo Mesogaias">Markopoulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koropi" title="Koropi">Koropi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spata" title="Spata">Spata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artemida,_Attica" title="Artemida, Attica">Loutsa</a>, about 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) to the east of central Athens (30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) by road, due to intervening hills). The airport is named after <a href="/wiki/Eleftherios_Venizelos" title="Eleftherios Venizelos">Elefth\xc3\xa9rios Veniz\xc3\xa9los</a>, the prominent Cretan political figure and Prime Minister of Greece, who made a significant contribution to the development of Greek aviation and the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Air_Force" title="Hellenic Air Force">Hellenic Air Force</a> in the 1930s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As to-date, the airport is operated by <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport_S.A." title="Athens International Airport S.A.">AIA S.A.</a> and ownership is divided between the Hellenic Republic (Greek State) and Private Sector in a 55%-45% stake following a <a href="/wiki/Public-private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-private partnership">PPP</a> scheme for the airport company.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Currently, private investors include the Copelouzos Group (5%)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Public_Sector_Pension_Investment_Board" title="Public Sector Pension Investment Board">PSP Investments</a> of Canada (40%), following purchase of <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a>\'s shares.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport was constructed to replace the now-closed <a href="/wiki/Ellinikon_International_Airport" title="Ellinikon International Airport">Athens (Ellinikon) International Airport</a>, as the latter had reached its saturation point with no physical space for further growth.<sup id="cite_ref-AW2010_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW2010-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Studies for a new airport had been carried out from as early as the 1970s, with as many as 19 different locations being looked at before an area close to the town of <a href="/wiki/Spata" title="Spata">Spata</a> was chosen as suitable.<sup id="cite_ref-AW2010_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW2010-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <i>Athens Airport SA</i>, a state-owned company, was established in 1978 to proceed with the plans. However, after delays and slow development, the project was revived in 1991 with the then government launching an international tender for the selection of a <a href="/wiki/Build%E2%80%93operate%E2%80%93transfer#BOOT_(build\xe2\x80\x93own\xe2\x80\x93operate\xe2\x80\x93transfer)" title="Build\xe2\x80\x93operate\xe2\x80\x93transfer">build-own-operate-transfer</a> partner for the airport project, with <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a> of Germany being selected.<sup id="cite_ref-AW2010_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW2010-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1996, <i>Athens International Airport S.A.</i> (AIA) was established as a <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public\xe2\x80\x93private partnership">Public\xe2\x80\x93private partnership</a> with a 30-year <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">concession</a> agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-AIA_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> That same year, the \xe2\x82\xac2.1 billion development finally began with an estimated completion date of February 2001. The airport construction was completed five months before schedule, but was delayed opening a month due to surface connections to <a href="/wiki/Attiki_Odos" title="Attiki Odos">Attiki Odos</a> not being completed.<sup id="cite_ref-AW2010_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW2010-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The airport officially opened on 28 March 2001.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Its major features include two parallel runways being 4&#160;km (2.5&#160;mi) and 3.8&#160;km (2.4&#160;mi) long respectively. The airport has received approval from the <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">European Aviation Safety Agency</a><sup id="cite_ref-A380EASAFAA_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380EASAFAA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a><sup id="cite_ref-A380EASAFAA_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380EASAFAA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> for take-offs and landings of the biggest passenger jet worldwide, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">A380</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A380EASAFAA_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A380EASAFAA-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The first ever A380 to visit \'Eleftherios Venizelos\' Athens International Airport made an emergency landing on 13 April 2011 for emergency medical reasons. The first scheduled A380 flight took place on 26 October 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Greek_government_debt-crisis_impact_.282009.E2.80.932013.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_government_debt-crisis_impact_(2009\xe2\x80\x932013)">Greek government debt-crisis impact (2009\xe2\x80\x932013)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Greek government debt-crisis impact (2009\xe2\x80\x932013)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">Greek government-debt crisis</a> reduced the overall passenger traffic of the airport for six consecutive years. Many long-haul airlines outright terminated service to the airport, while others chose to operate on a seasonal basis only, opting to terminate service during the winter months.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, these problems were further exacerbated by the closure of <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Airlines" title="Olympic Airlines">Olympic Airlines</a>, which operated many long-haul flights to and from the airport. In 2013, the airport handled just above 12.5 million passengers, 3.2% fewer than in 2012 and lower by approximately 25% when compared to 2007\'s traffic, which was the all-time-high at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-AIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Recovery_and_new_levels_of_passenger_traffic_.282014.E2.80.932015.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Recovery_and_new_levels_of_passenger_traffic_(2014\xe2\x80\x932015)">Recovery and new levels of passenger traffic (2014\xe2\x80\x932015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recovery and new levels of passenger traffic (2014\xe2\x80\x932015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>2014 signaled a strong recovery for the airport\'s passenger traffic and all statistical figures. More than ten new airlines started new flights to and from Athens. Aegean Airlines strengthened its network by 30% (with many more destinations scheduled for 2015) while Ryanair established a new base in the Athens Airport and added eight destinations. The airport company recorded an increase in passenger traffic in excess of 21% during 2014, reaching 15.1 million passengers, resulted both by new destinations but also by increased capacity offered on established ones. Characteristically, Singapore and Gulf Air resumed flights<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> while Emirates, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> fly more frequently to/from Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-airlineroute.net_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airlineroute.net-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Line</a> resumed their weekly flights and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> retained their seasonal schedules to/from USA with even more frequent connectivity. From 2017 onwards, year-round services to Singapore are going to resume after more than five years. Flights are going to be operated by <a href="/wiki/Scoot" title="Scoot">Scoot</a>.\n</p><p>According to AIA published statistics, total traffic for 2015 achieved an impressive performance reaching almost 18.1 million passengers, an all-time-record for the airport at that time, increased by 19% on year-over-year basis<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and by 1.55 million (+9.4%) the previous best, which was the pre-crisis year 2007. In addition, over the same period, aircraft traffic exhibited a solid growth of 14% year-over-year.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, in 2015 a significant rise (+38%) was recorded by transfer passengers, with the international to international transfer traffic marking an impressive increase (+60%) demonstrating the significant enhancement of the Athens airport connectivity.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Exceeding_twenty_million_passengers_.282016.E2.80.932018.29_and_beyond"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Exceeding_twenty_million_passengers_(2016\xe2\x80\x932018)_and_beyond">Exceeding twenty million passengers (2016\xe2\x80\x932018) and beyond</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Exceeding twenty million passengers (2016\xe2\x80\x932018) and beyond">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>2016 was a landmark year for the Athens International Airport, both for domestic and international destinations. Annual results reflected a solid performance for a third year in a row fueled by double-digit growth, this time passing the twenty million mark, increased by 10.7% on year-over-year basis.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Healthy growth continued in 2017 with the airport showing traffic increase of 8.6% to a total of 21.7 million passengers, yet another all-time record for the Athens airport.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> During 2018, the airport achieved yet another record high, reporting increased passenger traffic by 11% to more than 24.1 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Equally, aircraft traffic achieved a new record with a reported annual growth of 10.8% to 217,094 movements.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the first three quarters of 2019, the airport traffic shows signs of further increase with passenger numbers up by 6.5%<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> to 19.97 million passengers and aircraft movements up by 3.2%.\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg/220px-Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg/330px-Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg/440px-Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="607" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Check_in_area_-_Athens_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in-area</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg/220px-Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg/330px-Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg/440px-Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Athens_airport_waiting_area.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waiting-area</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport currently has two terminals, the main terminal and the satellite terminal accessible by an underground link from the main terminal.\nIt is designed to be extended in a modular approach over the ensuing years in order to accommodate increases in air travel. These extensions are planned in a six-phase framework. The first (and current) phase allowed the airport to accommodate 26 million passengers per year. When the airport originally opened, the current phase called for a capacity of only 16 million passengers per year; however, the capacity was able to increase without progressing to the next phase thanks to advanced IT logistics.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The sixth and final expansion phase will allow the airport to accommodate an annual traffic of 50 million passengers, with the current layout leaving enough space for five more terminals to be added.<sup id="cite_ref-AW2010_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW2010-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> As such, the parallel runway system currently in place has been designed to accommodate flight traffic with this high equivalent annual passenger load upon completion of the final expansion phase.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_Terminal">Main Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Main Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The main terminal building handles all intra-<a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen</a> flights, as well as several non-Schengen flights. All of the airport\'s 144 check-in desks are located in the Main Terminal and it has three separate levels, one for arrivals, one for departures and a food court level complete with a view of the eastern runway. Finally, the terminal is equipped with fourteen <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a> and eleven belt conveyors for luggage.\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Hall A</b> is used for flights to Non-schengen countries and Non-European countries.</li>\n<li><b>Hall B</b> handles flights to Intra-schengen countries as well as domestic services.</li></ul>\n<p>In March 2018, the Athens International Airport issued a tender for its first physical expansion, concerning the south wings of the main terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The tender called for a building expansion with a total area of approximately 14,950 square meters over five levels (levels 0 to 4). The construction company to build the expansion has been awarded in summer 2018 and the project is scheduled to be completed by mid-2019. It will add 18 more counter check-in decks as well as additional space for arrivals, departures, security and automated control gates, it will also add expanded shopping area and new lounges by mid-2020.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_Terminal">Satellite Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Satellite Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The satellite terminal has two levels, one for arrivals and the other for departures.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI1_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It is easily accessible through an underground link complete with moving walkways. The terminal is equipped with ten jet bridges and is capable of handling annual traffic of six million passengers.\n</p><p>In recent years its parking stands were utilized for long term storage of airliners, specifically two ex-<a href="/wiki/Olympic_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Airways">Olympic Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_340" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus 340">Airbus A340-300s</a> (both aircraft were transferred to its new owner in February 2017)<sup id="cite_ref-A340removal_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A340removal-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>-300ER of defunct Greek start-up carrier <a href="/wiki/SkyGreece_Airlines" title="SkyGreece Airlines">SkyGreece Airlines</a>. However, as of June 2017, the parking space of the satellite terminal is in full use for both Schengen and non-Schengen area flights and to accommodate increased traffic. From June 2017 some low-cost carriers were using it. On 24 May 2018, the Satellite Terminal officially restarted full operations. The airlines using it are <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easyjet" class="mw-redirect" title="Easyjet">Easyjet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transavia" title="Transavia">Transavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transavia_France" title="Transavia France">Transavia France</a>, <a href="/wiki/TUIfly_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly Belgium">TUIfly Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Transat" title="Air Transat">Air Transat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scoot" title="Scoot">Scoot</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Alexandroupoli_Airport" title="Alexandroupoli Airport">Alexandroupoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Alia_International_Airport" title="Queen Alia International Airport">Amman\xe2\x80\x93Queen Alia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona%E2%80%93El_Prat_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona\xe2\x80\x93El Prat Airport">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beirut%E2%80%93Rafic_Hariri_International_Airport" title="Beirut\xe2\x80\x93Rafic Hariri International Airport">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Nikola_Tesla_Airport" title="Belgrade Nikola Tesla Airport">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Guglielmo_Marconi_Airport" title="Bologna Guglielmo Marconi Airport">Bologna</a>, <a id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Athens International Airport is the largest and busiest airport in Greece. By the end of 2019, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">26th busiest airport in Europe</a> handling a total traffic of 25.57 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-AIA_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_statistics">Annual statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Annual statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours sortable" style="text-align:right;">\n<caption><b>Passenger, aircraft movement and cargo statistics at "El. data-file-height="491" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Athens_Airport_suburban_rail_and_metro_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Station\'s platforms</div></div></div>\n<p>A railway station is immediately adjacent to the airport terminal, accessible by an elevated walkway. <a href="/wiki/Athens_Metro" title="Athens Metro">Athens Metro</a> <a href="/wiki/Line_3_(Athens_Metro)" title="Line 3 (Athens Metro)">line 3</a> and the suburban railway service <a href="/wiki/Proastiakos#Athens" title="Proastiakos">Proastiakos</a> run trains to and from this station.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is accessible by the <a href="/wiki/Attiki_Odos" title="Attiki Odos">Attiki Odos</a> toll highway from the centre and northern Athens, Varis-Koropiou Avenue from the western part, Laurio Ave. from the South, and Spata-Loutsa Avenue from the East. A variety of parking options are available on site at the airport in three different <a href="/wiki/Parking_lots" class="mw-redirect" title="Parking lots">parking lots</a>. Located at the arrivals level, opposite the airport terminal, the airport offers short-term parking for up to five hours with 1,357 parking spaces available in lots P1 and P2.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Long-term parking is located across the airport\'s main access road (Attiki Odos) with 5,802 parking spaces in lot P3.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A free shuttle bus is available to transport passengers, while the lots are also accessible by foot to the terminal. Premium <a href="/wiki/Valet" title="Valet">valet</a> service is also offered at the Departures level by Entrance 3.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">Taxis</a> are available at the designated Taxi waiting area located by exit 3 of the arrivals level.<sup id="cite_ref-Taxi_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taxi-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Limousine" title="Limousine">Limousine</a> service is also available upon request by the inner curbside of the arrivals level between exits 3 and 4.<sup id="cite_ref-Taxi_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taxi-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Athens_Mass_Transit_System" title="Athens Mass Transit System">Four bus lines</a> (X93, X95, X96, X97)<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> connect directly to the Athens greater area, X95 starts from Syntagma square, X93 connects the airport to intercity bus stations (<a href="/wiki/KTEL_(Greece)" title="KTEL (Greece)">KTEL</a> <a href="/wiki/Athens_Peloponnese_Bus_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Athens Peloponnese Bus Station">Kifissos Bus Terminal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athens_Liosion_Bus_Station" title="Athens Liosion Bus Station">Liosion bus terminal</a>), X96 to Athens main port <a href="/wiki/Piraeus" title="Piraeus">Piraeus</a> and X97 to <a href="/wiki/Elliniko_metro_station" title="Elliniko metro station">Elliniko metro station</a> the Southern terminal of <a href="/wiki/Athens_Metro_Line_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Athens Metro Line 2">Line 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bus_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bus-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Buses disembark passengers at the departures level and depart from the arrivals level between exits 4 and 5.<sup id="cite_ref-Bus_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bus-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Regional bus services by <a href="/wiki/KTEL_(Greece)" title="KTEL (Greece)">KTEL Express</a> operate to the airport, currently connecting the airport to <a href="/wiki/Rafina" title="Rafina">Rafina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Markopoulo_Mesogaias" title="Markopoulo Mesogaias">Markopoulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lavrio" class="mw-redirect" title="Lavrio">Lavrio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalyvia_Thorikou" title="Kalyvia Thorikou">Kalyvia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keratea" title="Keratea">Keratea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bus_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bus-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retail_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Retail_Park.jpg/220px-Retail_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Retail_Park.jpg/330px-Retail_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Retail_Park.jpg/440px-Retail_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="287" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Retail_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the retail park</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Air" title="Olympic Air">Olympic Air</a> have their head office in Building 57 on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Olympic Air also has offices in Building 53A.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_and_Aviation_Safety_Board" title="Air Accident Investigation and Aviation Safety Board">Air Accident Investigation and Aviation Safety Board</a> has an office in Office 1311 in Building 11.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li>The Greek fast food company <a href="/wiki/Goody%27s_S.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Goody&#39;s S.A.">Goody\'s S.A.</a> has its head office in Building 14B.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sofitel" title="Sofitel">Sofitel</a> Hotel</li>\n<li>Retail Park</li>\n<li><span class="anchor" id="Robotic_security"></span>Two robotic systems, named Hercules and Ulysses, are used by the airport for the handling of potentially dangerous materials.  They were donated by the <a href="/wiki/Stavros_Niarchos_Foundation" title="Stavros Niarchos Foundation">Stavros Niarchos Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Athens_International_Airport_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Athens_International_Airport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 14 August 2005, <a href="/wiki/Helios_Airways_Flight_522" title="Helios Airways Flight 522">Helios Airways Flight 522</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> was a scheduled passenger flight of <a href="/wiki/Helios_Airways" title="Helios Airways">Helios Airways</a> that crashed into mountain north of <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">Marathon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Varnavas" title="Varnavas">Varnavas</a> 40&#160;km from Athens. All 115 passengers and 6 crew on board the aircraft were killed. This is the deadliest aviation disaster in Greek history.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Athens_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Greece" title="List of the busiest airports in Greece">List of the busiest airports in Greece</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Greece" title="Transport in Greece">Transport in Greece</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
